spec.ai.groups <[]object> min=1 max=8	# Groups in priority order, where each group defines a set of LLM providers. The priority determines the priority of the backend endpoints chosen. Note: provider names must be unique across all providers in all priority groups. Backend policies may target a specific provider by name using `targetRefs[].sectionName`. Example configuration with two priority groups: groups: - providers: - azureopenai: deploymentName: gpt-4o-mini apiVersion: 2024-02-15-preview endpoint: ai-gateway.openai.azure.com - providers: - azureopenai: deploymentName: gpt-4o-mini-2 apiVersion: 2024-02-15-preview endpoint: ai-gateway-2.openai.azure.com policies: auth: secretRef: name: azure-secret

spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.ai.promptCaching.cacheMessageOffset <integer> default=0 min=0	# Shifts the message cache point further back in the conversation. 0 (default) places it at the second-to-last message. Higher values move it N additional messages towards the start, clamped to bounds.

spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health <object>	# Settings for passive and active health checking.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health.eviction <object>	# Settings for evicting unhealthy backends.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health.eviction.consecutiveFailures <integer> format=int32 min=0	# Number of consecutive unhealthy responses required before the backend is evicted. For example, a value of 5 means the backend must receive 5 unhealthy responses in a row before being evicted. When both consecutiveFailures and healthThreshold are set, the backend is evicted when either condition is met. When neither is set, a single unhealthy response can trigger eviction.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health.eviction.duration <string> default="3s"	# Base time a backend should be evicted after being marked unhealthy. Subsequent evictions use multiplicative backoff (duration * times_evicted). If all endpoints are evicted, the load balancer falls back to returning evicted endpoints rather than failing entirely. If unset, defaults to `3s`.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health.eviction.healthThreshold <integer> format=int32 min=0 max=100	# EWMA health score threshold, from 0 to 100. When set, a backend is evicted only if its computed health drops below this value after an unhealthy response (e.g. 50 evicts when EWMA health falls below 50%). Unlike consecutiveFailures, this sliding-window average lets a single success delay eviction. If both are set, either condition evicts; if neither, a single unhealthy response evicts.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health.eviction.restoreHealth <integer> format=int32 min=0 max=100	# Health score from 0 to 100 assigned to a backend when it returns from eviction. For gradual recovery, set below 100; for full recovery immediately, set 100. If unset, the backend resumes with the health it had when evicted.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.health.unhealthyCondition <string> min=1 max=16384	# CEL expression that determines whether a response indicates an unhealthy backend. When the expression evaluates to true, the backend is considered unhealthy and may be evicted. For example, to evict on 5xx responses: `response.code >= 500`. When unset, any 5xx response, or a connection failure, is treated as unhealthy. This default lowers the backend's health score but does not trigger eviction on its own.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.http <object>	# Settings for managing HTTP requests to the backend
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.http.requestTimeout <string>	# Deadline for receiving a response from the backend.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.http.version <string> enum=HTTP1|HTTP2	# HTTP protocol version for backend connections. If unset, it is inferred: `Service` appProtocol, `HTTP2` for gRPC, the original protocol for plaintext HTTP, or `HTTP1` for HTTPS because clients often upgrade HTTPS to HTTP/2 even when the backend does not support it.

spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tcp.keepalive.interval <string>	# Time between keepalive probes. If unset, this defaults to 180s.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tcp.keepalive.retries <integer> format=int32 min=1 max=64	# Maximum number of keepalive probes to send before dropping the connection. If unset, this defaults to 9.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tcp.keepalive.time <string>	# Time a connection needs to be idle before keepalive probes start being sent. If unset, this defaults to 180s.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls <object>	# Settings for managing TLS connections to the backend When set, TLS is originated to the backend using the system trusted CA certificates, and SNI is inferred from the destination.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.alpnProtocols <[]string> min=1 max=16	# Application-Layer Protocol Negotiation (`ALPN`) value to use in the TLS handshake. If not present, defaults to `["h2", "http/1.1"]`.

spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.caCertificateRefs[].name <string> default=""	# Name of the referent
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.insecureSkipVerify <string> enum=All|Hostname	# Originates TLS but skips verification of the backend's certificate WARNING: insecure; only use if the risks are understood Modes: * `All` disables all TLS verification * `Hostname` trusts the CA certificate but ignores hostname/SAN mismatches. Still insecure; prefer `verifySubjectAltNames` where possible.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.keyExchangeGroups <[]string>	# Ordered list of key exchange groups for a TLS connection. For example: `X25519_MLKEM768,X25519`.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef <[]object> max=1	# Enables mutual TLS to the backend using `tls.key` and `tls.crt` from the referenced credential source (defaulting to a Kubernetes `Secret`). An optional `ca.cert`, if present, verifies the server certificate, but `caCertificateRefs` takes priority. If unspecified, no client certificate is used.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].group <string>	# API group of the referenced credential; empty selects the core API group
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].kind <string>	# Kind of the referenced credential; empty defaults to `Secret`
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].name <string> (required) min=1 max=253	# Name of the referenced credential
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.sni <string> pattern="^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?(\\.[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?)*$" min=1 max=253	# Server Name Indicator (`SNI`) to use in the TLS handshake. If unset, the `SNI` is automatically set based on the destination hostname.
spec.ai.groups[].providers[].policies.tls.verifySubjectAltNames <[]string> min=1 max=16	# Subject Alternative Names (`SAN`) to verify in the server certificate. If not present, the destination hostname is automatically used.

spec.mcp.targets[].selector.namespaces.matchExpressions[].values <[]string>	# values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.namespaces.matchLabels <map[string]string>	# matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.services <object>	# `services` is the label selector for which `Service` resources should be selected.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.services.matchExpressions <[]object>	# matchExpressions is a list of label selector requirements. The requirements are ANDed.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.services.matchExpressions[].key <string> (required)	# key is the label key that the selector applies to.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.services.matchExpressions[].operator <string> (required)	# operator represents a key's relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.services.matchExpressions[].values <[]string>	# values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.
spec.mcp.targets[].selector.services.matchLabels <map[string]string>	# matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.
spec.mcp.targets[].static <object>	# Static MCP destination. When connecting to in-cluster `Service` resources, it is recommended to use `selector` instead.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.backendRef <object>	# Namespace-local `Service` resource by name. When set, this replaces `host` only; `port`, `path`, and `protocol` remain configured on this target.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.backendRef.name <string> default=""	# Name of the referent
spec.mcp.targets[].static.host <string> min=1 max=256	# Hostname or IP address of the MCP target.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.path <string> min=1 max=1024	# URL path of the MCP target endpoint. Defaults to `"/sse"` for the `SSE` protocol or `"/mcp"` for the `StreamableHTTP` protocol if not specified.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies <object>	# Policies for communicating with this backend. Policies may also be set in `AgentgatewayPolicy`, or in the top-level `AgentgatewayBackend`. Policies are merged on a field-level basis, with order: `AgentgatewayPolicy` < `AgentgatewayBackend` < `AgentgatewayBackend` MCP (this field). This field may only be used with host-based static targets, not `backendRef`.

spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.auth.aws.assumeRole.sessionNameExpression <string> min=1 max=16384	# SessionNameExpression is a CEL expression evaluated against each request to produce the session name (RoleSessionName), for example `jwt.sub` or `request.headers["x-team"]`. If the expression does not produce a valid session name at request time, the request is rejected.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.auth.aws.assumeRole.tags <[]object> max=50	# Session tags passed to STS AssumeRole for cost attribution in the AWS Cost & Usage Report, once activated. STS allows at most 50 per role session.

spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls <object>	# Settings for managing TLS connections to the backend When set, TLS is originated to the backend using the system trusted CA certificates, and SNI is inferred from the destination.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.alpnProtocols <[]string> min=1 max=16	# Application-Layer Protocol Negotiation (`ALPN`) value to use in the TLS handshake. If not present, defaults to `["h2", "http/1.1"]`.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.caCertificateRefs <[]object> max=1	# CA certificate `ConfigMap` to use to verify the server certificate. If unset, the system's trusted certificates are used.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.caCertificateRefs[].name <string> default=""	# Name of the referent
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.insecureSkipVerify <string> enum=All|Hostname	# Originates TLS but skips verification of the backend's certificate WARNING: insecure; only use if the risks are understood Modes: * `All` disables all TLS verification * `Hostname` trusts the CA certificate but ignores hostname/SAN mismatches. Still insecure; prefer `verifySubjectAltNames` where possible.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.keyExchangeGroups <[]string>	# Ordered list of key exchange groups for a TLS connection. For example: `X25519_MLKEM768,X25519`.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef <[]object> max=1	# Enables mutual TLS to the backend using `tls.key` and `tls.crt` from the referenced credential source (defaulting to a Kubernetes `Secret`). An optional `ca.cert`, if present, verifies the server certificate, but `caCertificateRefs` takes priority. If unspecified, no client certificate is used.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].group <string>	# API group of the referenced credential; empty selects the core API group
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].kind <string>	# Kind of the referenced credential; empty defaults to `Secret`

spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.sni <string> pattern="^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?(\\.[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?)*$" min=1 max=253	# Server Name Indicator (`SNI`) to use in the TLS handshake. If unset, the `SNI` is automatically set based on the destination hostname.
spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tls.verifySubjectAltNames <[]string> min=1 max=16	# Subject Alternative Names (`SAN`) to verify in the server certificate. If not present, the destination hostname is automatically used.

spec.mcp.targets[].static.policies.tunnel.backendRef <object> (required)	# Proxy server to reach. Supported types: `Service` and `Backend`.

spec.policies.ai.promptCaching.cacheMessageOffset <integer> default=0 min=0	# Shifts the message cache point further back in the conversation. 0 (default) places it at the second-to-last message. Higher values move it N additional messages towards the start, clamped to bounds.
spec.policies.ai.promptCaching.cacheMessages <boolean> default=true	# Enables caching for conversation messages. Caches all messages in the conversation for cost savings.

spec.policies.ai.promptCaching.minTokens <integer> default=1024 min=0	# Minimum estimated token count before caching is enabled. Uses rough heuristic (word count × 1.3) to estimate tokens. Bedrock requires at least 1,024 tokens for caching to be effective.

spec.policies.extAuth.cache <object>	# Caches authorization results. WARNING: the safety of this feature depends on the cache key accurately capturing every request property that the authorization service uses to make a decision. For example, if the service returns different results based on both path and authorization header, both must be included in `key`; otherwise, one request may incorrectly reuse another request's authorization result. If any key expression fails to evaluate or produces an unsupported value, the request is still sent to the authorization service, but its result is not read from or written to the cache.
spec.policies.extAuth.cache.key <[]string> (required) min=1 max=16	# Ordered list of CEL expressions evaluated against the request to construct the cache key.
spec.policies.extAuth.cache.maxEntries <integer> format=int32 min=1	# Maximum number of authorization results to keep in the cache. If unset, this defaults to 10000.
spec.policies.extAuth.cache.ttl <string> (required) min=1 max=16384	# Duration string, such as `5m`, or a CEL expression that returns the duration that cached authorization results may be reused, or a timestamp when the cached authorization result expires. The expression is evaluated after the authorization response has been applied to the request.
spec.policies.extAuth.failureMode <string> enum=FailClosed|FailOpen	# Behavior when the external authorization service is unavailable or returns an error. "FailOpen" allows the request to continue. "FailClosed" (default) denies the request.
spec.policies.extAuth.forwardBody <object>	# Whether to include the HTTP body in the authorization request. If enabled, the request body will be buffered.
spec.policies.extAuth.forwardBody.maxSize <int-or-string> (required)	# Largest body, in bytes, that will be buffered and sent to the authorization server. If the body size is larger than `maxSize`, then the request will be rejected with a response.
spec.policies.extAuth.grpc <object>	# Uses the gRPC External Authorization [protocol](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/api-v3/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto) should be used.
spec.policies.extAuth.grpc.contextExtensions <map[string]string>	# Additional arbitrary key-value pairs to send to the authorization server in the `context_extensions` field.
spec.policies.extAuth.grpc.requestMetadata <map[string]string>	# Metadata to send to the authorization server. This maps to the `metadata_context.filter_metadata` field of the request, and allows dynamic CEL expressions. If unset, by default the `envoy.filters.http.jwt_authn` key is set if the JWT policy is used as well, for compatibility.
spec.policies.extAuth.http <object>	# Uses HTTP to connect to the authorization server. The authorization server must return a `200` status code, otherwise the request is considered an authorization failure.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.addRequestHeaders <map[string]string>	# Additional headers to add to the request to the authorization server. While `allowedRequestHeaders` just passes the original headers through, `addRequestHeaders` allows defining custom headers based on CEL expressions.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.allowedRequestHeaders <[]string> max=64	# Additional headers from the client request that will be sent to the authorization server. If unset, the following headers are sent by default: `Authorization`.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.allowedResponseHeaders <[]string> max=64	# Headers from the authorization response that will be copied into the request to the backend.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.body <string> min=1 max=16384	# Body is a CEL expression that produces the HTTP authorization request body. Strings and bytes are used directly; other values are JSON-encoded.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.path <string> min=1 max=16384	# Path to send to the authorization server. If unset, this defaults to the original request path. This is a CEL expression, which allows customizing the path based on the incoming request. For example, to add a prefix, use `"/prefix/" + request.path`.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.redirect <string> min=1 max=16384	# Optional expression that determines a path to redirect to on authorization failure. This is useful to redirect to a sign-in page.
spec.policies.extAuth.http.responseMetadata <map[string]string>	# Metadata fields to construct from the authorization response. These will be included under the `extauthz` variable in future CEL expressions. Setting this is useful for things like logging usernames, without needing to include them as headers to the backend, as `allowedResponseHeaders` would.
spec.policies.health <object>	# Settings for passive and active health checking.
spec.policies.health.eviction <object>	# Settings for evicting unhealthy backends.
spec.policies.health.eviction.consecutiveFailures <integer> format=int32 min=0	# Number of consecutive unhealthy responses required before the backend is evicted. For example, a value of 5 means the backend must receive 5 unhealthy responses in a row before being evicted. When both consecutiveFailures and healthThreshold are set, the backend is evicted when either condition is met. When neither is set, a single unhealthy response can trigger eviction.
spec.policies.health.eviction.duration <string> default="3s"	# Base time a backend should be evicted after being marked unhealthy. Subsequent evictions use multiplicative backoff (duration * times_evicted). If all endpoints are evicted, the load balancer falls back to returning evicted endpoints rather than failing entirely. If unset, defaults to `3s`.
spec.policies.health.eviction.healthThreshold <integer> format=int32 min=0 max=100	# EWMA health score threshold, from 0 to 100. When set, a backend is evicted only if its computed health drops below this value after an unhealthy response (e.g. 50 evicts when EWMA health falls below 50%). Unlike consecutiveFailures, this sliding-window average lets a single success delay eviction. If both are set, either condition evicts; if neither, a single unhealthy response evicts.
spec.policies.health.eviction.restoreHealth <integer> format=int32 min=0 max=100	# Health score from 0 to 100 assigned to a backend when it returns from eviction. For gradual recovery, set below 100; for full recovery immediately, set 100. If unset, the backend resumes with the health it had when evicted.
spec.policies.health.unhealthyCondition <string> min=1 max=16384	# CEL expression that determines whether a response indicates an unhealthy backend. When the expression evaluates to true, the backend is considered unhealthy and may be evicted. For example, to evict on 5xx responses: `response.code >= 500`. When unset, any 5xx response, or a connection failure, is treated as unhealthy. This default lowers the backend's health score but does not trigger eviction on its own.
spec.policies.http <object>	# Settings for managing HTTP requests to the backend
spec.policies.http.requestTimeout <string>	# Deadline for receiving a response from the backend.
spec.policies.http.version <string> enum=HTTP1|HTTP2	# HTTP protocol version for backend connections. If unset, it is inferred: `Service` appProtocol, `HTTP2` for gRPC, the original protocol for plaintext HTTP, or `HTTP1` for HTTPS because clients often upgrade HTTPS to HTTP/2 even when the backend does not support it.
spec.policies.mcp <object>	# Settings for MCP workloads. This is only applicable when connecting to a `Backend` of type `mcp`.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication <object>	# MCP backend-specific authentication rules. This field is deprecated; prefer to use traffic policy `jwtAuthentication.mcp`, which ensures authentication runs before other policies such as transformation and rate limiting.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.audiences <[]string> min=1 max=64	# Allowed audiences that are allowed access. This corresponds to the `aud` claim ([RFC 7519 §4.1.3](https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7519#section-4.1.3)). If unset, any audience is allowed.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.clientId <string>	# Client ID to use for short-circuiting Dynamic Client Registration. If set, the gateway will not proxy registration requests to the IDP and instead return this client ID.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.issuer <string> min=1 max=256	# IdP that issued the JWT. This corresponds to the `iss` claim ([RFC 7519 §4.1.1](https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7519#section-4.1.1)).
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks <object> (required)	# Remote JSON Web Key used to validate the signature of the JWT.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.backendRef <object> (required)	# Remote JWKS server to reach. Supported types are `Service` and static `Backend`. An `AgentgatewayPolicy` containing backend TLS config can then be attached to the `Service` or `Backend` in order to set TLS options for a connection to the remote `jwks` source.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.backendRef.group <string> default="" pattern="^$|^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?(\\.[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?)*$" max=253	# Group of the referent, for example `gateway.networking.k8s.io`. Empty selects the core API group
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.backendRef.kind <string> default="Service" pattern="^[a-zA-Z]([-a-zA-Z0-9]*[a-zA-Z0-9])?$" min=1 max=63	# Kubernetes resource kind of the referent, for example `Service`. Defaults to `Service`
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.backendRef.name <string> (required) min=1 max=253	# Name is the name of the referent.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.backendRef.namespace <string> pattern="^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?$" min=1 max=63	# Namespace of the referent. Defaults to the local namespace. A cross-namespace reference requires a ReferenceGrant in the referent namespace
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.backendRef.port <integer> format=int32 min=1 max=65535	# Destination port number. Required when the referent is a Kubernetes `Service`
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.cacheDuration <string> default="5m"
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.jwks.jwksPath <string> (required) min=1 max=2000	# Path to the IdP `jwks` endpoint, relative to the root, commonly `".well-known/jwks.json"`.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.mode <string> enum=Optional|Permissive|Strict default="Strict"	# Validation mode for JWT authentication.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.provider <string> enum=Auth0|Authentik|Descope|Keycloak|Okta	# Identity provider to use for authentication.
spec.policies.mcp.authentication.resourceMetadata <object (free-form)>	# Metadata to use for MCP resources.
spec.policies.mcp.authorization <object>	# MCP backend authorization. Unlike authorization at the HTTP level, which rejects unauthorized requests with a `403` error, this policy works at the `MCPBackend` level. List operations, such as `list_tools`, will have each item evaluated. Items that do not meet the rule will be filtered. Get or call operations, such as `call_tool`, will evaluate the specific item and reject requests that do not meet the rule.
spec.policies.mcp.authorization.action <string> enum=Allow|Deny|Require default="Allow"	# The effect of this rule when it matches. If unspecified, defaults to `Allow`. `Require` rules are cumulative: all require rules must match.
spec.policies.mcp.authorization.policy <object> (required)	# The authorization rule to evaluate. * `Allow`: any matching allow rule allows the request. * `Require`: every require rule must match for the request to be allowed. * `Deny`: any matching deny rule denies the request. A CEL expression that fails to evaluate does not match. Prefer `Require` for deny-by-default behavior. If at least one `Allow` rule is configured, requests are denied unless at least one allow rule matches.
spec.policies.mcp.authorization.policy.matchExpressions <[]string> (required) min=1 max=256	# CEL expressions that must all evaluate to true for the rule to match.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails <object>	# `guardrails` routes selected JSON-RPC methods through a remote policy server.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors <[]object> (required) min=1 max=16	# `processors` is the ordered list of policy processors applied to matched methods. Processors run in the order listed; the first to reject a request short-circuits the chain.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].methods <map[string]string> (required)	# `methods` is the allowlist of JSON-RPC methods (e.g. `tools/call`, `tools/list`) routed through this processor, keyed by method name with the phase it runs in. Keys may be exact, a prefix wildcard (`tools/*`), a suffix wildcard (`*/list`), or `*` for all methods; the most specific match wins. Methods matching no key, including unknown ones, bypass this processor.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote <object>	# `remote` configures a gRPC policy server.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.allowedRequestHeaders <[]string> max=64	# `allowedRequestHeaders` lists the incoming request headers forwarded to the policy server in `McpRequest.headers`. If empty, all headers and pseudo-headers (`:authority`, `:method`, ...) are forwarded. Matching is case-insensitive.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.backendRef <object> (required)	# `backendRef` references the remote guardrails policy server. Supported types: `Service` and `Backend`.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.backendRef.group <string> default="" pattern="^$|^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?(\\.[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?)*$" max=253	# Group of the referent, for example `gateway.networking.k8s.io`. Empty selects the core API group
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.backendRef.kind <string> default="Service" pattern="^[a-zA-Z]([-a-zA-Z0-9]*[a-zA-Z0-9])?$" min=1 max=63	# Kubernetes resource kind of the referent, for example `Service`. Defaults to `Service`
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.backendRef.name <string> (required) min=1 max=253	# Name is the name of the referent.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.backendRef.namespace <string> pattern="^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?$" min=1 max=63	# Namespace of the referent. Defaults to the local namespace. A cross-namespace reference requires a ReferenceGrant in the referent namespace
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.backendRef.port <integer> format=int32 min=1 max=65535	# Destination port number. Required when the referent is a Kubernetes `Service`
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.disallowedRequestHeaders <[]string> max=64	# `disallowedRequestHeaders` lists header names never forwarded to the policy server, even if listed in `allowedRequestHeaders`. Matching is case-insensitive.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.failureMode <string> enum=FailClosed|FailOpen	# `failureMode` controls behavior when the policy server is unreachable or returns an error. `FailOpen` allows the request; `FailClosed` (default) denies it.
spec.policies.mcp.guardrails.processors[].remote.metadata <map[string]string>	# `metadata` is static or CEL-evaluated context surfaced to the policy server as fields of the `metadata_context` google.protobuf.Struct, keyed by config key. Values are CEL expressions.
spec.policies.tcp <object>	# Settings for managing TCP connections to the backend

spec.policies.tcp.keepalive <object>	# Settings for enabling TCP keepalives on the connection.
spec.policies.tcp.keepalive.interval <string>	# Time between keepalive probes. If unset, this defaults to 180s.
spec.policies.tcp.keepalive.retries <integer> format=int32 min=1 max=64	# Maximum number of keepalive probes to send before dropping the connection. If unset, this defaults to 9.
spec.policies.tcp.keepalive.time <string>	# Time a connection needs to be idle before keepalive probes start being sent. If unset, this defaults to 180s.
spec.policies.tls <object>	# Settings for managing TLS connections to the backend When set, TLS is originated to the backend using the system trusted CA certificates, and SNI is inferred from the destination.
spec.policies.tls.alpnProtocols <[]string> min=1 max=16	# Application-Layer Protocol Negotiation (`ALPN`) value to use in the TLS handshake. If not present, defaults to `["h2", "http/1.1"]`.
spec.policies.tls.caCertificateRefs <[]object> max=1	# CA certificate `ConfigMap` to use to verify the server certificate. If unset, the system's trusted certificates are used.
spec.policies.tls.caCertificateRefs[].name <string> default=""	# Name of the referent
spec.policies.tls.insecureSkipVerify <string> enum=All|Hostname	# Originates TLS but skips verification of the backend's certificate WARNING: insecure; only use if the risks are understood Modes: * `All` disables all TLS verification * `Hostname` trusts the CA certificate but ignores hostname/SAN mismatches. Still insecure; prefer `verifySubjectAltNames` where possible.
spec.policies.tls.keyExchangeGroups <[]string>	# Ordered list of key exchange groups for a TLS connection. For example: `X25519_MLKEM768,X25519`.
spec.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef <[]object> max=1	# Enables mutual TLS to the backend using `tls.key` and `tls.crt` from the referenced credential source (defaulting to a Kubernetes `Secret`). An optional `ca.cert`, if present, verifies the server certificate, but `caCertificateRefs` takes priority. If unspecified, no client certificate is used.
spec.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].group <string>	# API group of the referenced credential; empty selects the core API group
spec.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].kind <string>	# Kind of the referenced credential; empty defaults to `Secret`
spec.policies.tls.mtlsCertificateRef[].name <string> (required) min=1 max=253	# Name of the referenced credential
spec.policies.tls.sni <string> pattern="^[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?(\\.[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?)*$" min=1 max=253	# Server Name Indicator (`SNI`) to use in the TLS handshake. If unset, the `SNI` is automatically set based on the destination hostname.
spec.policies.tls.verifySubjectAltNames <[]string> min=1 max=16	# Subject Alternative Names (`SAN`) to verify in the server certificate. If not present, the destination hostname is automatically used.

status <object>	# Current backend status.
status.conditions <[]object> max=8	# Current condition state for the backend.
status.conditions[].lastTransitionTime <string> (required) format=date-time	# lastTransitionTime is the last time the condition transitioned from one status to another. This should be when the underlying condition changed. If that is not known, then using the time when the API field changed is acceptable.
status.conditions[].message <string> (required) max=32768	# message is a human readable message indicating details about the transition. This may be an empty string.
status.conditions[].observedGeneration <integer> format=int64 min=0	# observedGeneration represents the .metadata.generation that the condition was set based upon. For instance, if .metadata.generation is currently 12, but the .status.conditions[x].observedGeneration is 9, the condition is out of date with respect to the current state of the instance.
status.conditions[].reason <string> (required) pattern="^[A-Za-z]([A-Za-z0-9_,:]*[A-Za-z0-9_])?$" min=1 max=1024	# reason contains a programmatic identifier indicating the reason for the condition's last transition. Producers of specific condition types may define expected values and meanings for this field, and whether the values are considered a guaranteed API. The value should be a CamelCase string. This field may not be empty.
status.conditions[].status <string> (required) enum=True|False|Unknown	# status of the condition, one of True, False, Unknown.
status.conditions[].type <string> (required) pattern="^([a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?(\\.[a-z0-9]([-a-z0-9]*[a-z0-9])?)*/)?(([A-Za-z0-9][-A-Za-z0-9_.]*)?[A-Za-z0-9])$" max=316	# type of condition in CamelCase or in foo.example.com/CamelCase.
